**Prompt truncation — top-3 memories + top-3 error patterns + max 80 chars each:** post-Epic-11.7, audit finding **P2-9** closes architecturally. Pre-11-7 `buildConversationPrompt` at `src/lib/prompts/conversation.ts:23` had a single shared `MAX_PROMPT_USER_ITEMS = 20` count cap and NO per-item char cap — so a long-tenure user with 20 memories at 300 chars each + 20 error patterns at 300 chars each pushed ~12,000 chars (~3,000 tokens) of user-derived content into the Realtime system prompt on top of the ~2,500-token base prompt. At `gpt-realtime-mini` rates (Story 11-5) that added ~$0.00003/turn × 30-60 turns/session = ~$0.001-$0.0018/session in prompt-tax, AND ~144-288ms of TTFT (time-to-first-token) prefill latency at the front of every session + every Story 11-2 reconnect (cached `RealtimeConfig.systemPrompt` is replayed verbatim on reconnect). Three new exported constants in `conversation.ts` enforce the bound: `MAX_PROMPT_MEMORIES = 3` + `MAX_PROMPT_ERROR_PATTERNS = 3` (per-block count caps, replacing the deleted shared `MAX_PROMPT_USER_ITEMS`) + `MAX_PROMPT_ITEM_CHARS = 80` (per-item byte cap, PROMPT-INJECTION-ONLY — does NOT affect `sanitizeMemoryContent`'s `MAX_MEMORY_CHARS = 300` storage cap at the write boundary). New pure helper `truncateToBytes(text, max)` exported from the same module: predictable hard slice (no ellipsis, no word-boundary heuristics) with two defensive guards mirroring `sanitizeMemoryContent`'s logic at `src/lib/memory.ts:175-181` — (1) surrogate-pair backoff (cut that would split a UTF-16 high surrogate like an emoji 🎉 backs off by 1 to avoid emitting a lone surrogate that breaks JSON/UTF-8), (2) partial-marker tail strip (cut landing inside a `[redacted:...]` injection-redaction marker strips the partial fragment + trimEnd). The two injection blocks (`<USER_FACTS>` + `<USER_WEAK_AREAS>`) now use the pipeline `sanitize → filter-empty → slice(N) → truncate → filter-empty`: sanitize-FIRST preserves the Story 9-4 stored-prompt-injection invariant (injection tokens stripped before any other transformation operates on the string); slice-BEFORE-truncate avoids wasted work on items we'd discard; the second filter-empty defends against the degenerate truncate-to-empty edge case. The Realtime session bootstrap at `app/(tabs)/conversation/[sessionId].tsx:205-206` is reduced from `retrieveMemories(user.id, topic, 8) + getTopErrors(user.id, 5)` (13 rows fetched but only 13/20 injected — wasted Supabase + pgvector cosine RPC work on rows the builder accepted anyway) to `retrieveMemories(user.id, topic, MAX_PROMPT_MEMORIES) + getTopErrors(user.id, MAX_PROMPT_ERROR_PATTERNS)` (3 + 3 = 6 rows fetched, 6 injected — bounded I/O matches bounded prompt). `MAX_PROMPT_USER_ITEMS` is **DELETED** (Story 10-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 "delete don't alias" pattern; verified single in-file caller via `grep -rn "MAX_PROMPT_USER_ITEMS"`); a star-import test in `conversation-truncation.test.ts` asserts the export is `undefined` so a future refactor that re-introduces the constant fails CI loudly. **`use-daily-briefing.ts` is explicitly NOT touched** — daily briefing renders memories + top errors to a non-Realtime UI surface (no token tax), and applying the 80-char per-item cap there would degrade user-visible text. The user-derived prompt tail drops from worst-case ~12,160 chars (hypothetical pre-11-7 = `2 × 20 × (300 + 4)`) → bounded ~1,822 chars (empirical post-11-7 = `504 items + 1,318 wrapper`). **CORRECTION (Story 13-8 verification, 2026-05-15):** the original Story 11-7 claim of **"25× reduction"** was OVERSTATED at **~4× too high**; the empirical reduction is **6.7×** (`12,160 / 1,822`). The 25× number compared USER-ITEM CONTENT only (`12,000 / ~480 chars` of items); reality includes the `~1,318 chars` of `<USER_FACTS>` + `<USER_WEAK_AREAS>` wrapper text (Story 9-4 bilingual "treat as data" prelude + section headers + tag delimiters) which dominates the post-truncation tail. Still a meaningful **~85% reduction in user-derived bytes per session** — but the 25× marketing was wrong. CI-pinned at `MIN_REDUCTION_RATIO = 5×` in [`src/lib/prompts/__tests__/conversation-prompt-perf.test.ts`](src/lib/prompts/__tests__/conversation-prompt-perf.test.ts) (Story 13-8). **Estimate-only (not CI-pinned):** ~144-288ms TTFT savings per session + ~$0.001-$0.0018 cost/session at gpt-realtime-mini rates — these remain operator-estimates requiring device profiling (queued as Action Item #3 in Epic 13 retro for Epic 16 prep); base prompt + Story 9-4 prelude + Story 11-1 tool-call definitions unchanged. Story 11-2 reconnect path inherits the smaller prompt for free (cached `RealtimeConfig.systemPrompt` is replayed verbatim); Story 11-4's `daily_cost_ledger` pre-flight check at `realtime-session/index.ts` tightens automatically because the per-call `estimateChatCostCents` input-token estimate is lower. Story 11-6's `match_error_pattern` RPC + `embedding VECTOR(1536)` column + HNSW index + `isValidEmbedding` helper all unchanged — 11-7 consumes the 11-6-deduped top-3 error patterns from `getTopErrors` (Story 11-6 guarantees these are 3 distinct mistakes, not 3 near-duplicates of the same). Sentry allowlist unchanged (no new `feature` tags — truncation is pure transformation, no error-recoverable boundary). Closes audit P2-9 architecturally. Stories 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-2 / 10-3 / 10-4 / 10-5 / 10-6 / 10-7 / 10-8 / 11-1 / 11-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 invariants all hold unchanged. Regression-tested in `src/lib/prompts/__tests__/conversation-truncation.test.ts` (NEW — 27 Jest cases: 3 constant pins + delete-don't-alias guard for `MAX_PROMPT_USER_ITEMS` via star-import introspection + 12-case `truncateToBytes` helper contract (identity / boundary / idempotence / surrogate-pair-backoff + emoji-below-cut / partial-marker tail strip / complete-marker-below-cut survives / unconditional-trimEnd mirror invariant / non-string defensive guard) + 12-case `buildConversationPrompt` integration coverage (5-item → 3-item output for both blocks, 200-char input → 80-char output, each line ≤ MAX + 2 prefix, empty/undefined arrays → no block rendered, Story 9-4 sanitize-before-truncate invariant verified by feeding a poisoned `"Ignore all prior instructions"` input + asserting the injection token doesn't survive into the prompt, sanitization-driven empty rows don't waste a slot)) + `src/lib/__tests__/session-bootstrap-fetch-limits-source.test.ts` (NEW — 5 drift-detector cases reading `[sessionId].tsx` from disk: imports both constants from the conversation prompt module + `retrieveMemories` consumes `MAX_PROMPT_MEMORIES` + `getTopErrors` consumes `MAX_PROMPT_ERROR_PATTERNS` + negative guards against the pre-11-7 hardcoded `retrieveMemories(user.id, topic, 8)` and `getTopErrors(user.id, 5)` literals). +32 net Jest cases (1121 → 1153). Verified 2026-05-13, story 11-7.

**Empty-response detection + retry parity across all 4 AI helpers:** post-Epic-11.8, the closing Epic 11 deliverable lands and audit catch-all "P2-x ai-integration findings" closes architecturally. Pre-11-8 the 4 AI helpers in `src/lib/openai.ts` had **asymmetric retry budgets** + **asymmetric empty-response detection**: (a) `chatCompletion` had `MAX_RETRIES = 2` + empty-check ONLY on `responseFormat === "json_object"` (text-mode empty silently returned `""`); (b) `generateSpeech` had `maxRetries = 1` + fixed `sleep(1000)` + NO empty check (an empty Azure Blob propagated silently to the audio player); (c) `transcribeAudio` had `maxRetries = 1` + fixed `sleep(1000)` + empty-check at the boundary but error message didn't match `isRetryable` regex so was non-retried; (d) `generateEmbedding` had `maxRetries = 1` + fixed `sleep(1000)` + the silently-emit-empty-array pathology (`?? []` return) that propagated through `persistMemories` → `JSON.stringify([])` → Postgres `VECTOR(1536)` cast rejection (delayed write-failure noise; Story 11-6's `isValidEmbedding` was the consumer-side mitigation). Post-11-8 all 4 helpers consume two shared exported constants from `openai.ts` — `MAX_RETRIES = 2` + `RETRY_DELAYS: readonly number[] = [1000, 2000]` — with one source of truth so a future operator change propagates atomically (Story 10-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 "delete don't alias" pattern as applied to numeric constants; the 3 local `const maxRetries = 1` + 3 fixed `sleep(1000)` literals are deleted from `generateSpeech` / `transcribeAudio` / `generateEmbedding`). `chatCompletion`'s empty-check at line 105-107 is broadened from the json-object gate to `typeof content !== "string" || content.trim().length === 0` (catches null / undefined / empty string / whitespace-only across both text and JSON modes). `generateSpeech` gains an empty-Blob check (`bytes.length === 0` after `data.arrayBuffer()`) + an empty-string fallback check; throws `"Empty TTS response"`. `transcribeAudio`'s pre-existing `"Empty transcription response"` throw stays unchanged. `generateEmbedding` replaces the silent `?? []` return with an explicit `!Array.isArray(embedding) || embedding.length === 0` boundary check that throws `"Empty embedding response"` — the two-layer embedding defense is preserved: this coarse-grain "non-empty array" gate at the boundary plus Story 11-6's `isValidEmbedding` consumer-side check at `error-tracker.ts` (verifies `length === 1536` + every component is finite). `isRetryable` at line 23-47 is extended with one new `msg.includes("empty")` branch so all 4 of the canonical error messages — `"Empty AI response"` / `"Empty TTS response"` / `"Empty transcription response"` / `"Empty embedding response"` — match the retry predicate; an upstream 200-with-empty-body stutter is now recovered by the retry loop instead of surfacing as a user-visible failure. Stacking math with Story 11-3's server-side `fetchWithTimeout` (30s for chat / TTS / embedding / realtime-session / pronunciation; 90s for Whisper): worst-case end-to-end latency for a chat call = `(MAX_RETRIES + 1) × per-attempt-timeout + Σ RETRY_DELAYS = 3 × 30s + (1s + 2s) = 93s` (unchanged for chat); for TTS / Whisper / embedding the worst-case bumps from `2 × per-attempt + 1s` to `3 × per-attempt + 3s` (~32s additional for TTS / embeddings; ~94s additional for Whisper). Acceptable trade-off per the reliability win. Story 11-4's `daily_cost_ledger` pre-flight runs per attempt; retried attempts each re-charge cost — pre-11-8 behavior preserved for chat, new for TTS / Whisper / embedding (per-call cost is tiny: ~$0.000006 for embeddings, ~$0.001 for TTS at 200 chars; failed-call frequency < 0.1% per provider SLAs so cap-tax impact is bounded). Story 9-7's `chatCompletionJSON.parseRetries` layer is ABOVE this network retry layer; parse-retries default 1, network-retries default `MAX_RETRIES = 2`. Both stay; no semantic collision (a schema parse failure on attempt 1 → retry whole chain which may itself burn 2 network retries per pass). Sentry allowlist unchanged (no new `feature` strings — control flow only). Stories 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-2 / 10-3 / 10-4 / 10-5 / 10-6 / 10-7 / 10-8 / 11-1 / 11-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 invariants all hold unchanged. Closes Epic 11 (audit findings P1-6 / P1-7 / P1-8 / P1-9 / P1-10 / P1-21 / P2-1 / P2-9 / P2-x ai-integration all resolved). Regression-tested in `src/lib/__tests__/openai-retry-parity.test.ts` (NEW — 15 Jest cases: 3 constant pins + 2 `isRetryable` source-content checks + 10 drift-detector cases reading `openai.ts` from disk and pinning per-helper `MAX_RETRIES` consumption + `RETRY_DELAYS[attempt]` schedule consumption + negative guards against pre-11-8 `const maxRetries = 1` and fixed `sleep(1000)` literals + `chatCompletion` empty-check covers all modes + `generateEmbedding` throws-on-empty + `generateSpeech` empty-Blob throw + `transcribeAudio` empty-text throw preserved + constants exported) + `src/lib/__tests__/openai-empty-response.test.ts` (NEW — 18 runtime cases via mocked `supabase.functions.invoke` driving each helper's empty-response code path: `chatCompletion` text + JSON + whitespace + null + happy + 1-retry-recovery; `generateSpeech` empty Blob + empty-string fallback + happy; `transcribeAudio` empty text + missing field + happy; `generateEmbedding` undefined + empty array + missing field + non-array + happy 1536-dim + 2-layer-defense short-array passes the coarse-grain boundary). +33 net Jest cases (1159 → 1192). Verified 2026-05-13, story 11-8. **Story 11-8 review-round-1 patches** (HIGH × 3 + MED × 5 + LOW × 2; P11 deferred — operator-attempt-count Sentry signal requires Story 9-3 allowlist extension that's out of scope for this round): P1 `isRetryable` `msg.includes("empty")` substring match narrowed to exact-match against the canonical `RETRYABLE_EMPTY_MESSAGES = Set([4 sentinels])` allowlist — pre-patch a benign error like `"OpenAI error: empty quota"` or `"Empty request body — 400"` would have spuriously retried 2× wasting cost-cap budget on non-recoverable errors; P2 explicit `Array.isArray(data?.data)` shape guard in `generateEmbedding` BEFORE indexing `data.data[0]?.embedding` — future upstream shape-drift like `data: { data: null }` or `data: { data: {} }` no longer slips through to a misleading "Empty embedding response" with no shape-error signal; P3 drift detector regex `\bconst\s+maxRetries\s*=\s*1\s*[;\n]` replaces the pre-patch `const maxRetries = 1[^0-9]` — formatter quirks producing double-space or missing-space-around-equals can no longer mask a regression; P4 `globalThis.setTimeout` shim install/restore moved from `beforeAll`/`afterAll` to `beforeEach`/`afterEach` for per-test isolation — pre-patch an `afterAll` failure (unhandled rejection mid-suite) would leak the immediate-callback shim across concurrent test files in the same Jest worker; P5 "two-layer defense" test now imports `isValidEmbedding` from `error-tracker.ts` and proves it returns `false` on the same 5-element array the boundary accepts (and `true` on a valid 1536-dim array) — pre-patch the comment claimed the two-layer contract but never exercised it, so a future refactor removing Story 11-6's consumer guard wouldn't fail this test; P6 the 3 helper JSDocs no longer hardcode the literal `2` retry count — they reference `MAX_RETRIES (see constant above)` so a future operator bump propagates cleanly; P7 `RETRY_DELAYS` is `Object.freeze`'d + a frozen-contract test pins `Object.isFrozen(RETRY_DELAYS) === true` and asserts `RETRY_DELAYS.push(4000)` throws — pre-patch a consumer mutation could have silently corrupted the schedule globally for all 4 helpers; P8 `isRetryable` is now exported + a parameterized 22-case `it.each` matrix asserts runtime retryability for the 4 canonical sentinels (uppercase + lowercase variants), pre-11-8 retryable substrings (network/timeout/fetch/5xx/429/rate-limit), P1 over-match negative guards ("OpenAI error: empty quota" / "Empty request body — 400" / "Authentication failed: empty token cookie" / "Empty cache miss" all `=== false`), unrelated errors, and non-Error inputs; P9 `chatCompletion`'s empty-response detection switched from `.trim().length === 0` to `!/\S/u.test(content)` — Unicode whitespace categories (NBSP U+00A0, line separator U+2028, paragraph separator U+2029) are now detected as empty (pre-patch `.trim()` is ASCII-whitespace-only on older JS engines); P10 dropped the `?? ""` default at `data?.choices?.[0]?.message?.content` so the post-coercion `typeof content !== "string"` check becomes meaningful (pre-patch the default made the typeof branch dead code; a future refactor removing `?? ""` would have silently mis-handled non-string upstream values). +30 net Jest cases (1192 → 1222 — 7 frozen-RETRY_DELAYS + P9 Unicode-whitespace cases on the parity file; 22 isRetryable runtime contract cases; 1 P5 two-layer defense cross-check). Verified 2026-05-13, story 11-8 (post-review-round-1 patches HIGH × 3 + MED × 5 + LOW × 2).

**Realtime voice god-hook decomposition + persistConversation parallelization:** post-Epic-12.1, audit finding **P1-17** closes architecturally. Pre-12-1 `src/hooks/use-realtime-voice.ts` was a **1,354-line god-hook** running 14 responsibilities (16 `useRef`s + a `useState` for state, WebSocket connection lifecycle, ExpoPlayAudioStream subscription, the 430-line `handleEvent` switch routing 12+ Realtime event types, Story 11-1's `handleFunctionCall` for 3 tool-call types — `save_vocabulary` + `note_error_pattern` + `report_correction`, `appendAiTranscriptEntry` + Story 9-5 dedup, `correctionsRef` + Story 11-1 `pendingToolCorrections` orphan buffer, AI-speaking state tracking + Story 11-2 barge-in timing, `createConversationRecord`, the 180-line `persistConversation` 8-step chain, duration tracking, inflight response tracking, reconnect state coordination, offline queue fallback) — far over the CLAUDE.md 200-line component guideline AND the audit-spec'd `useRealtimeVoice.ts ≤ 250 lines` target. The hook had grown ~70% since the original P1-17 filing (794 → 1,354 lines) through Stories 11-1 / 11-2 / 11-5 / 11-8 additions. Story 12-1 extracts the 14 responsibilities into a new **plain TypeScript class** `RealtimeOrchestrator` at `src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts` (~1,025 lines, including absorbed JSDoc + the per-event handlers split for readability: `handleSpeechStarted` / `handleItemCreated` / `handleResponseDone` / `handleErrorEvent` / `handleReconnecting`). The orchestrator uses an **observer pattern** for state propagation: `subscribe(callback): () => void` returns an unsubscribe closure, mirroring Story 11-2's `RealtimeSession.on(event)` pattern so operator mental model is symmetric across both `lib/` classes. Internal `setState(updater)` is the sole state-mutation point — fires all subscribers synchronously (with a snapshot to defend against subscribers unsubscribing mid-iteration) AND synchronously updates the `isAiSpeakingMirror` private field (Story 11-2 review-round-2 P22 lesson — synchronous mirror is required for event-time barge-in detection because React's setState commit lags real-event ordering). Public surface: `start()` / `sendText(text)` / `end()` / `subscribe(cb)` / `getState()` / `dispose()`. The hook at `src/hooks/use-realtime-voice.ts` shrinks from **1,354 → 116 lines (8.7× reduction; 53% under the 250-line spec budget)** — purely a React binding: lazy-construct the orchestrator on first render via `useRef`, `useState` mirroring the orchestrator's `ConversationState`, `useEffect` subscribing to the orchestrator + cleaning up on unmount via `dispose()`, `useCallback`-wrapped pass-through methods. The public hook API (`UseRealtimeVoiceOptions` + `UseRealtimeVoiceReturn`) is **IDENTICAL** to pre-12-1 — `app/(tabs)/conversation/[sessionId].tsx` consumes the hook with **zero changes**. The 8-step `persistConversation` chain parallelizes into **Phase A** (6 independent slots dispatched concurrently via `Promise.allSettled`: `conversation` update + `messages` insert + AI `analysis` + `skill-progress` + `daily-activity` + `streak`) + **Phase B** (`checkCefrPromotion` AFTER Phase A because it reads the `skill_progress` row updated by the skill-progress slot — running it in parallel would race against the UPDATE and read stale data). `PHASE_A_SLOT_NAMES` constant exported from the orchestrator pins the slot names for test invariance + Sentry tag construction (`persist-conversation-phase-a-${slot}` for per-slot failure isolation; Phase B uses `persist-conversation-cefr-promotion`). Per-slot failure isolation matches Story 11-5's `persistPostConversationAnalysis` pattern: rejected `Promise.allSettled` slots route through `captureError(_, "feature")`; supabase-fulfilled-with-error slots (Story 11-5 review patch P3 pattern) ALSO route through `captureError` because supabase-js v2 resolves with `{ data, error }` on Postgres-side failures without rejecting the promise. Pre-12-1 tail latency = sum of 8 sequential awaits ≈ 4,400ms; post-12-1 = `max(Phase A 6-parallel) + Phase B ≈ 3,000ms + 300ms = 3,300ms` (~25% reduction; the AI call dominates Phase A's max, so the absolute Supabase-write savings is ~1.1s). Sibling-story carve-outs explicitly preserved: 12-3 atomic-RPC mutations operates on the orchestrator's Phase A slots (replaces per-row Supabase round-trips with `UPDATE x = x + $1` server-side RPCs); 12-4 `sessionRef = session before connect()` race fix operates on the orchestrator's `start()` method; 12-5 ExpoPlayAudioStream singleton operates on the orchestrator's `startAudioStreaming`/`stopAudioStreaming`; 12-6 transcriptRef 200-entry cap operates on the orchestrator's private `transcript` field. The orchestrator is **directly unit-testable without a React renderer** — `new RealtimeOrchestrator(opts); orchestrator.subscribe(...)` extends Story 11-2's `RealtimeSession.test.ts` testability pattern. Stories 9-3 (Sentry allowlist preserved — no new feature tags beyond the 7 new `persist-conversation-phase-a-{slot}` + `persist-conversation-cefr-promotion` tags, all short categorical under 80 chars) / 9-4 (`buildConversationPrompt` `<USER_FACTS>` + `<USER_WEAK_AREAS>` wrapping unchanged) / 9-5 (`appendIfNew` + `acceptDelta` + `resolveTranscriptKey` pure helpers from `realtime-transcript.ts` called at the same boundary) / 9-6 (auth listener orthogonal; orchestrator captures `user` at construction time) / 9-7 (`chatCompletionJSON` `parseRetries` contract preserved via `extractPostConversationAnalysis`) / 9-8 + 10-6 (speaking pipeline separate `chatCompletionJSON(speakingTaskEvaluationSchema)` flow not touched) / 9-9 (deploy substrate orthogonal) / 9-10 (auth + cache race orthogonal) / 10-X (prompts + scoring + dedup orthogonal) / 11-1 (`processReportCorrectionCall` + `drainPendingCorrections` + `mergeOrphanCorrections` pure helpers from `realtime-corrections.ts` called at the same boundaries; P2/P3 orphan-drain on response.done + case "error" + realtime.reconnecting all preserved by construction in `handleResponseDone` / `handleErrorEvent` / `handleReconnecting`) / 11-2 (`computeBargeInDirective` from `realtime-barge-in.ts` + `RealtimeSession` event subscriptions + per-turn refs migrated to class fields with identical semantics; review-round-2 P22 synchronous `isAiSpeakingMirror` mirror + P24 don't-stop-audio-on-reconnect + P25 start guards against reconnecting + P28 benign barge-in race suppression + P30 clear `currentAiText` on barge-in all preserved) / 11-3 (`fetchWithTimeout` orthogonal — server-side) / 11-4 (Postgres rate-limit + cost cap orthogonal) / 11-5 (`extractPostConversationAnalysis` + `persistPostConversationAnalysis` + `gpt-realtime-mini` MODEL unchanged; **Auth listener one-time bootstrap + pure-consumer `useAuth` hook:** post-Epic-12.2, audit finding **P0-7 deepening** closes architecturally. Pre-12-2, `useAuth()` was called by **7 different consumers** (`app/_layout.tsx`, `app/(tabs)/profile/settings.tsx`, `app/(tabs)/profile/index.tsx`, `app/(auth)/login.tsx`, `app/(auth)/signup.tsx`, `app/onboarding/placement-test.tsx`, `app/onboarding/index.tsx`) and each invocation installed its own `supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange` listener inside `useEffect` — meaning any auth event (e.g., `SIGNED_IN`, `INITIAL_SESSION`, `USER_UPDATED`) fan-out to N concurrent listener bodies that each ran `decideAuthAction` + dispatched `loadProfile(userId)` against the same userId, producing N concurrent `cacheWithFallback` calls + N concurrent Supabase `profiles.select(...)` queries + N concurrent `flushWriteQueue` invocations. Story 9-6's `flushWriteQueue` idempotency Promise-gate (`let inFlight: Promise<number> | null = null`) caught the duplicated flushes downstream but `loadProfile` itself was NOT module-scope idempotent — N concurrent profile-fetch + cache-write races executed in full. Additionally, **Story 9-10's `profileFetchFailed` flag could race**: listener A's failed loadProfile sets `setProfileFetchFailed(true)`; listener B's successful loadProfile (same auth event, parallel dispatch) overwrites it with `false`, masking real failures from `ProfileRetryScreen`. Story 12-2 collapses the fan-out to 1 via **`src/lib/auth-bootstrap.ts`** — a new module with: (a) `bootstrapAuth(): () => void` idempotent installer guarded by module-level `let bootstrapState: { teardown: () => void } | null = null` (mirrors Story 9-6's `flushWriteQueue` `let inFlight` pattern; second call returns the SAME teardown closure without re-subscribing), (b) the migrated `decideAuthAction`-dispatch listener + cold-start `supabase.auth.getSession()` + `loadProfile(userId, opts)` + `retryProfileFetch()` from the deleted hook `useEffect`, (c) **static module-level action exports** (`signInWithEmail` / `signUpWithEmail` / `signOut` / `updateProfile` / `retryProfileFetch`) that read user from `useAuthStore.getState().user` directly — no React state captured, no per-render closure allocation, (d) `__resetBootstrapForTests()` `@internal` escape hatch for test isolation (pattern matches Story 11-2's `_triggerStateChange`). `app/_layout.tsx` invokes `bootstrapAuth()` at **module-load time (top-level, outside the component body)** so the listener installs synchronously during JS bundle parse — BEFORE any React render. **The `useAuth()` hook shrinks from 359 → 70 lines (5.1× reduction; 12.5% under the 80-line budget)** as a pure consumer: 6 per-field `useAuthStore((s) => s.X)` selectors + re-exported static action methods. `applyProfileIfFresh` moves into `auth-bootstrap.ts` (where `loadProfile` lives) and is RE-EXPORTED from `use-auth.ts` to preserve the existing test import path at `src/lib/__tests__/auth-load-profile-stale.test.ts` (Story 9-10). **All 7 consumer call sites compile with zero changes** — the public `UseAuthReturn` shape is preserved verbatim. Pre-12-2 the hook's `useAuthStore()` single destructure caused re-renders on ANY store-field change; post-12-2 per-field selectors fire re-renders only on the consumed field change (Zustand idiom). Story 9-6 invariants preserved by construction (the listener body is the same `decideAuthAction`-switch with `load-profile` / `clear-profile` / `session-only` / `no-session-warning` cases). Story 9-10 invariants preserved by construction (`applyProfileIfFresh` userId-guard + `profileFetchFailed` flag + `flushWriteQueue` idempotency all flow through unchanged — the race that 9-6's downstream guard caught is now caught UPSTREAM at the subscription level). Story 12-1's `RealtimeOrchestrator`'s `useAuthStore.getState().user` read continues working unchanged (orchestrator reads from the store directly, not via the hook). Sentry allowlist unchanged (no new `feature` strings — preserves pre-12-2 `auth-initial-session` + `auth-load-profile` tags verbatim). Closes audit P0-7 deepening architecturally. Stories 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-2 / 10-3 / 10-4 / 10-5 / 10-6 / 10-7 / 10-8 / 11-1 / 11-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 invariants all hold unchanged. Regression-tested in `src/lib/__tests__/auth-bootstrap.test.ts` (NEW — 17 Jest cases: bootstrap idempotence × 5 [single subscription on first call + 2 sequential calls install only ONE + same teardown returned + teardown invocation calls unsubscribe + `__resetBootstrapForTests` clears singleton] + Story 9-6 per-event branching × 6 [INITIAL_SESSION → cacheWithFallback fires + USER_UPDATED → invalidateCache + loadProfile (flushQueue: false) + SIGNED_OUT → setProfile(null) + setProfileFetchFailed(false) + setLoading(false) + TOKEN_REFRESHED → setSession only + PASSWORD_RECOVERY → session-only + null session on TOKEN_REFRESHED → no-session breadcrumb] + Story 9-10 userId-guard × 2 [catch path sets flag when fresh + does NOT set flag when user changes mid-flight via cacheWithFallback mock that clears the store user before throwing] + retryProfileFetch shape × 2 [no-op without user + calls cacheWithFallback with flushQueue: false] + cold-start getSession × 2 [called exactly once + safety-net setLoading(false) on no-session]) + `src/hooks/__tests__/use-auth.test.tsx` (NEW — 6 react-test-renderer hook-binding cases: hook does NOT call bootstrapAuth itself + verbatim UseAuthReturn shape + action method identity stable across renders + store state propagation + multiple HookHost consumers do NOT install N listeners + action methods forward through to bootstrap-module imports) + `src/hooks/__tests__/use-auth-line-budget.test.ts` (NEW — 8 drift-detector cases reading `use-auth.ts` from disk: line count ≤ 80 + sanity floor + imports from auth-bootstrap + negative guards [no `useEffect` + no direct supabase import + no `onAuthStateChange` + no `getSession`] + per-field selector count ≥ 6; uses `HOOK_CODE_ONLY` (block + line comments stripped) so JSDoc that mentions pre-12-2 surfaces doesn't trip the negative-guards). +31 net Jest cases (1260 → 1291). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-2. **Story 12-2 review-round-1 patches** (HIGH × 5 + MED × 5 + LOW × 5): P1 re-entrancy guard — `bootstrapState` is set to a sentinel BEFORE `supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange` is called so a re-entrant `bootstrapAuth()` call during listener install (e.g., a future module pulled in transitively by `decideAuthAction` calls bootstrap) sees the in-progress state and returns the shared teardown instead of re-subscribing; P2 cold-start race defense — the `getSession().then` safety-net `setLoading(false)` gate is widened from `if (!session)` to `if (!session && !useAuthStore.getState().session)` so a `getSession` that resolves with `null` AFTER the listener installed a session (network blip / cache expiry between calls) no longer prematurely clears loading while `loadProfile` is still in flight; P3 Jest module-load guard — `app/_layout.tsx` wraps the top-level `bootstrapAuth()` call in `if (typeof process === "undefined" || !process.env.JEST_WORKER_ID)` so a future test that imports `_layout.tsx` transitively does not execute the real supabase client's `onAuthStateChange` at module-parse time before per-test `jest.mock` factories install; P4 Metro Fast Refresh / HMR dispose — `module.hot.dispose` registers a teardown so a hot-swap of `auth-bootstrap.ts` in dev tears down the previous subscription before the new module installs a fresh one, preventing stale listeners from accumulating monotonically across file saves (wrapped in `try/catch` because `module.hot` is not present in production or Jest); P5 `__resetBootstrapForTests` microtask drain — converted to `async` + `await Promise.resolve()` twice so a prior test's fire-and-forget `void loadProfile(...)` whose `cacheWithFallback` resolves on the next microtask completes BEFORE the next test's `beforeEach` installs fresh mocks (pre-patch a sync reset left dangling continuations that would mutate the next test's store + mock state invisibly); P6 idempotent teardown + closure-staleness defense — the returned teardown closure now tracks `let alreadyTornDown = false` + nullifies the `capturedSubscription` reference after first invocation so a future `__resetBootstrapForTests` → new bootstrap → call-old-teardown path does not double-unsubscribe an already-dead subscription handle; P7 `try/catch` on `onAuthStateChange` install — wraps the call so a synchronous throw from the supabase client (broken state from prior `signOut` failure, SDK upgrade introducing throws) is captured via `captureError(_, "auth-bootstrap-install")` + the bootstrap degrades gracefully to a no-op teardown instead of blocking app start at JS bundle parse with no error UI; P8 drift-detector regex tolerates type annotations — `useAuthStore\(\((?:s|state)(?:\s*:\s*\w+)?\)\s*=>\s*\w+\.[a-zA-Z]+\)` replaces the brittle `useAuthStore\(\(s\)\s*=>\s*s\.[a-zA-Z]+\)` so a benign refactor adding `(s: AuthState) =>` annotations or renaming `s` to `state` doesn't silently drop the per-field-selector count below 6 and fail CI; P9 removed dead `applyProfileIfFresh` mock from `use-auth.test.tsx`'s `jest.mock("@/src/lib/auth-bootstrap", ...)` factory — the hook re-exports `applyProfileIfFresh` but never invokes it (production `loadProfile` calls the local function inside `auth-bootstrap.ts` directly, not via the import shim), so the mocked value was dead code; P10 added `MFA_CHALLENGE_VERIFIED → session-only` test case (Case 10b) — `auth-events.test.ts` covers the `decideAuthAction` helper for this event but pre-patch the bootstrap test had no case that would fail if a future refactor accidentally dropped MFA from the listener body's `case "session-only":` branch (e.g., misplaced fall-through); P11 `__resetBootstrapForTests` runtime test-only guard — `if (typeof process !== "undefined" && process.env.NODE_ENV !== "test") throw new Error(...)` so accidental production invocation fails loudly (the `@internal` JSDoc was advisory-only and could be ignored by any caller); P12 StrictMode JSDoc correction — pre-patch the comment claimed "defensive against React StrictMode double-mount" but StrictMode only re-runs component bodies, never module top-level; corrected to "defensive against the rare case of a consumer accidentally invoking `bootstrapAuth()` from a `useEffect`" + the new P4 HMR-dispose context; P13 `mockGetSession` `mockReset` + re-default in `beforeEach` — pre-patch `mockClear` alone preserved the default `.mockResolvedValue` but a previous test's `.mockResolvedValueOnce` override consumed mid-suite would leave the next test inheriting whatever followed in the queue (typically undefined); now `mockReset()` + re-install the canonical no-session resolution each `beforeEach`; P14 `mockOnAuthStateChange` capture-array — replaces the scalar `registeredCallback` with an array `registeredCallbacks` + `getRegisteredCallback()` accessor (returns last element) so a future refactor that accidentally double-subscribes (the exact bug 12-2 is preventing) but only retains the last reference fails the new `expect(registeredCallbacks).toHaveLength(1)` assertion in Case 2; P15 `_layout.tsx` load-bearing-ordering comment — documents that `Sentry.init(getSentryInitConfig())` MUST precede `bootstrapAuth()` because `captureError` inside the bootstrap routes through Sentry; without init, those captures would no-op. **Deferred (10 pre-existing items not introduced by 12-2):** useAuth fresh-object-literal-each-render (pre-12-2 had same pattern; all 7 consumers verified not destructuring into useMemo deps), auth-store reset race with listener clear-profile branch, signOut clearUserCache fire-and-forget privacy concern, updateProfile silent error swallow when both data + error are null, retryProfileFetch racing user state change, no teardown on root unmount (partially addressed by P4), signInWithEmail vs signUpWithEmail return-shape asymmetry, signOut concurrent-call race, auth-load-profile-stale.test.ts import path future risk, cold-start setLoading double-call wasted work. **5 rejected** as noise: 2 Blind Hunter low-impact + 4 Acceptance Auditor "no action required" LOW findings. +1 net Jest case (1291 → 1292 — the new MFA case). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-2 (post-review-round-1 patches HIGH × 5 + MED × 5 + LOW × 5).

**Atomic Postgres RPCs for activity-mutation races:** post-Epic-12.3, audit finding **P1-18** closes architecturally. Pre-12-3 `src/lib/activity.ts` had 4 helpers — `updateStreak` / `updateSkillProgress` / `incrementDailyActivity` / `checkCefrPromotion` — each implementing a **client-side SELECT-then-UPDATE** pipeline that is NOT atomic against the Postgres row: two concurrent callers (phone + web in the upcoming paid tier) both read the same pre-update state, both compute `prev + delta`, both write — silently dropping ONE increment per race. The bug was already documented at [`activity.ts:100-104`](src/lib/activity.ts#L100-L104) and [`activity.ts:310-314`](src/lib/activity.ts#L310-L314) via two `TODO(epic-10-schema-hardening)` JSDoc markers ("read-modify-write pattern below is not atomic ... Fix requires either an RPC with `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` or a Postgres function that does the running-avg math server-side"). Story 12-3 lands that fix. New forward-only migration `supabase/migrations/20260514000000_atomic_activity_rpcs.sql` adds **4 RPC functions**: (1) `update_streak_atomic(p_user_id, p_today, p_yesterday) → INTEGER` — single-statement `UPDATE profiles SET streak_days = CASE ... END` with the today / yesterday / reset branches inlined; row-level lock acquired by the UPDATE serializes concurrent callers, second observes the post-first state and the `WHEN last_active_date = p_today THEN streak_days` arm short-circuits (no double-increment). (2) `update_skill_progress_atomic(p_user_id, p_skill, p_cefr_level, p_incoming_score, p_time_minutes) → VOID` — `INSERT INTO skill_progress ... ON CONFLICT (user_id, skill) DO UPDATE SET score = round(((skill_progress.score * skill_progress.exercises_completed) + EXCLUDED.score) / (skill_progress.exercises_completed + 1)::numeric), exercises_completed = skill_progress.exercises_completed + 1, total_time_minutes = skill_progress.total_time_minutes + EXCLUDED.total_time_minutes, cefr_level = CASE WHEN array_position(...EXCLUDED.cefr_level) > array_position(...skill_progress.cefr_level) THEN EXCLUDED.cefr_level ELSE skill_progress.cefr_level END` — running-average math + Story 9-2's no-regress CEFR rule (B2 row + A1 review keeps B2) run server-side inside one statement; row-lock on conflict resolution serializes concurrent writes by definition. Score is clamped to [0, 100] server-side via `GREATEST(0, LEAST(100, COALESCE(p_incoming_score, 0)))` as belt-and-braces; client also clamps via `clampScore` so malformed input is caught at the boundary. (3) `increment_daily_activity_atomic(p_user_id, p_date, p_minutes, p_exercises, p_conversations, p_words) → VOID` — `INSERT INTO daily_activity ... ON CONFLICT (user_id, date) DO UPDATE SET minutes_practiced = daily_activity.minutes_practiced + EXCLUDED.minutes_practiced` for each of the 4 counters; both deltas land under contention. (4) `promote_cefr_level_atomic(p_user_id, p_expected_current_level, p_next_level) → BOOLEAN` — **compare-and-swap** UPDATE `WHERE id = p_user_id AND current_cefr_level = p_expected_current_level`; `GET DIAGNOSTICS v_rows_updated = ROW_COUNT` then `RETURN v_rows_updated = 1` — TRUE on swap landed, FALSE if a concurrent worker promoted first (in which case the client silently returns; the next promotion check re-evaluates from the post-promotion state). The pre-step pipeline for `checkCefrPromotion` (SELECT current*cefr_level + SELECT skill_progress rows + `evaluatePromotion`) stays client-side because `evaluatePromotion` is Story 9-2's pure decision helper exhaustively unit-tested. All 4 functions are **`SECURITY DEFINER` + `SET search_path = public`** (Story 9-9 hardening) + an `IF auth.uid() IS DISTINCT FROM p_user_id THEN RAISE EXCEPTION` defense-in-depth check (Story 9-9 verified pattern from `check_and_increment_rate_limit` / `match_error_pattern`) + `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM PUBLIC` + `GRANT EXECUTE TO authenticated`. The 4 client-side helpers in `src/lib/activity.ts` are **rewritten** to call `supabase.rpc("update_streak_atomic", ...)` / `supabase.rpc("update_skill_progress_atomic", ...)` / `supabase.rpc("increment_daily_activity_atomic", ...)` / `supabase.rpc("promote_cefr_level_atomic", ...)` instead of the prior SELECT-then-UPDATE round trips — **mobile-network round-trip count drops from 2 per call × 4 callers = 8 round-trips per typical activity tick to 1 per call × 4 = 4 round-trips per tick** (material latency improvement on Phase A's tail-latency budget). The 2 `TODO(epic-10-schema-hardening)` JSDoc markers are **DELETED** — Story 10-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 / 12-2 "delete don't alias" pattern, the debt is paid down at the schema layer. Unused `maxLevel` helper in `activity.ts` (only used by pre-12-3 `updateSkillProgress`) is **DELETED** (lint-clean by construction). All pure helpers stay unchanged: `getLocalDateString`, `evaluatePromotion`, `clampScore`, `isCEFRLevel`, `PromotionEvidence`, `PromotionDecision`, `PASSING_SCORE`, `MIN_PASSING_SKILLS`, `MIN_TOTAL_EXERCISES`, `TCF_SKILLS_IN_ORDER`, `lastSkippedBreadcrumb` — Story 9-2's `evaluatePromotion` test block (`activity.test.ts`) stays green by construction. Public API surface of the 4 helpers preserved verbatim — all 8 caller files (`use-exercise.ts`, `use-echo-practice.ts`, `use-translation.ts`, `use-dictation.ts`, `use-progress.ts`, `app/(tabs)/mock-test/[testId].tsx`, `src/lib/speaking-mock-test-persist.ts`, `src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts`) compile with zero changes. **Fail-OPEN policy** on RPC error: each helper's catch block routes through `captureError(*, "feature-tag")` with the 4 pre-12-3 Sentry tags preserved (`update-streak`, `update-skill-progress`, `increment-daily-activity`, `cefr-promotion`— Story 9-3 allowlist contract; no new tags). Activity tracking is fire-and-forget from Story 12-1's Phase A`Promise.allSettled`— never block the user-facing flow on a tracking-pipeline write failure (Story 11-4 pattern). The`getLocalDateString`(Story 9-2's local-timezone fix) stays **client-side** — today + yesterday are passed as DATE params to the RPCs; switching to Postgres`CURRENT_DATE` would silently break streaks for non-UTC users by reverting to UTC. Story 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-X / 11-1 / 11-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 / 12-2 invariants all hold unchanged. Closes audit P1-18 architecturally. Closes Epic 12 AC at [`shippable-roadmap.md`line 219](_bmad-output/planning-artifacts/shippable-roadmap.md) ("Concurrent phone+web session test does not lose any increments (verified via 100 concurrent updates)") via the new pgTAP-style 100-concurrent-update test. Regression-tested in `src/lib/\_\_tests\_\_/atomic-activity-rpcs-migration-drift.test.ts` (NEW — 15 Jest drift-detector cases reading the SQL migration from disk: 4 function-name pins +`SECURITY DEFINER`× 4 pin +`SET search_path = public`× 4 pin +`auth.uid() IS DISTINCT FROM p_user_id`defense-in-depth × 4 pin +`RAISE EXCEPTION`× 4 pin +`REVOKE EXECUTE ... FROM PUBLIC`× 4 pin +`GRANT EXECUTE ... TO authenticated`× 4 pin +`update_streak_atomic`CASE-branches pin (today / yesterday / reset arms) +`update_skill_progress_atomic` `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (user_id, skill) DO UPDATE` row-lock pin + running-average math pattern pin (`skill_progress.score \* skill_progress.exercises_completed + EXCLUDED.score / skill_progress.exercises_completed + 1`) + no-regress CEFR rule via `array_position(ARRAY[...], EXCLUDED.cefr_level)`pin +`GREATEST(0, LEAST(100, COALESCE(...)))`server-side clamp pin +`increment_daily_activity_atomic` `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (user_id, date) DO UPDATE`+ 4 cumulative-add pattern pins +`promote_cefr_level_atomic`compare-and-swap WHERE clause pin +`GET DIAGNOSTICS v_rows_updated = ROW_COUNT`+`RETURN v_rows_updated = 1`pin + idempotent migration safety (no`DROP TABLE`/`DROP COLUMN`) + `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION`× 4 + bare`CREATE FUNCTION === 0` + audit traceability (`Story 12-3`+`P1-18`references)) + `src/lib/\_\_tests\_\_/activity-rpc-mutations.test.ts` (NEW — 16 Jest rpc-mock contract cases:`updateStreak`× 4 (single-call dispatch with correct args + Sentry tag on error + sync-throw fail-OPEN + no fallback to`from("profiles")`); `updateSkillProgress`× 4 (correct args including clamped score + out-of-range clamp [150→100, -25→0] + NaN→0 + Sentry tag with skill/score/cefrLevel extras);`incrementDailyActivity`× 3 (all 4 deltas + today + missing fields default to 0 + Sentry tag);`checkCefrPromotion`× 5 (passing decision →`promote_cefr_level_atomic`dispatched with A1/A2 + CAS FALSE silent path no captureError + Sentry tag on error with level extras + non-promoting outcome → addBreadcrumb fires + NO RPC dispatched + C2 short-circuit no RPC no breadcrumb)) + `supabase/migrations/\_\_tests\_\_/atomic_activity_rpcs_test.sql` (NEW — 11 manual-run pgTAP-style assertions: streak happy path + 100-concurrent → streak_days=1 no overcounting + skill_progress insert + running-avg update + no-regress CEFR + 100-concurrent same-score → exercises=100 score=80 no losses + daily_activity insert + cumulative add + 100-concurrent → minutes=100 no losses + promote_cefr_level happy path A1→A2 + CAS mismatch returns FALSE no stale write + auth.uid() cross-user defense-in-depth raises + GRANT EXECUTE TO authenticated present; manual-run via`psql -f`, NOT CI-wired — Epic 15.3 scope). +31 net Jest cases (1292 → 1323). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-3. **Story 12-3 review-round-1 patches** (HIGH × 3 + MED × 8 + LOW × 6): P1 no-regress CEFR rule COALESCEs the stored-side `array_position`so a NULL or out-of-list`skill_progress.cefr_level`(corruption from a legacy migration, pre-CHECK-constraint era, etc.) no longer evaluates to NULL → falls-to-ELSE → bogus-value-preserved-forever; both array_position lookups are now`COALESCE(array_position(...), 0)`so an incoming valid level wins via the strict-greater-than comparison; P2`update_streak_atomic`+`promote_cefr_level_atomic`both`RAISE EXCEPTION 'profile not found for user_id %', p_user_id USING ERRCODE = 'no_data_found'`when the profile row doesn't exist — pre-patch the UPDATE-not-found returned NULL silently and the client wrapper only checked`error`not`data`, masking a user with a failed profile-creation-trigger forever; `promote_cefr_level_atomic` now explicitly distinguishes "row missing" (raise) from "CAS-mismatch" (return FALSE) via a pre-`SELECT EXISTS`check; P3 pgTAP test header rewritten to clarify the "100 concurrent" assertions are SEQUENTIAL math-contract verification (single connection, single transaction, row lock acquired+released between calls) and do NOT exercise real cross-connection row-level locking — the Epic 12 AC ("verified via 100 concurrent updates") is satisfied ARCHITECTURALLY by`INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`row-lock semantics + DETERMINISTICALLY by this test; actual concurrent-connection verification deferred to Epic 15.3 with a`pgbench -c 100 -j 100 -t 1`invocation example documented; P4`update_skill_progress_atomic`validates`p_cefr_level NOT IN ('A1','A2','B1','B2','C1','C2')`at function entry — defense-in-depth against the missing CHECK constraint on`skill_progress.cefr_level`in the initial schema; P5 fresh INSERT branch now wraps`round(p_incoming_score)`symmetric with the ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE running-avg`round(...)`so pre- and post-12-3 rows have stable integer-rounded semantics — pre-patch a fresh INSERT with 95.5 would land as 95.5 while the same row's next update would round; P6`checkCefrPromotion`FALSE-CAS-mismatch path now emits an info-level`addBreadcrumb({ category: "cefr-promotion", level: "info", message: "cefr-promotion-raced (concurrent worker won the CAS)", data: { fromLevel, toLevel } })`instead of falling through to the success path that cleared`lastSkippedBreadcrumb`— pre-patch a CAS race was misclassified as a successful promotion in observability; the throttle is NOT cleared on FALSE because the user did not actually advance via this worker; P7`promote_cefr_level_atomic`validates`p_next_level NOT IN ('A1','A2','B1','B2','C1','C2')`at function entry with a clear error message — defense-in-depth on top of the`profiles.current_cefr_level`CHECK constraint; P8 drift detector regex for`array_position`loosened from the strict`array_position\(\s*ARRAY\['A1','A2','B1','B2','C1','C2'\],\s*EXCLUDED\.cefr_level`to`array_position\(\s*ARRAY\s*\[\s*'A1'\s*,\s*'A2'\s*,\s*'B1'\s*,\s*'B2'\s*,\s*'C1'\s*,\s*'C2'\s*\]\s*,\s*EXCLUDED\.cefr_level`so a prettier auto-format that wraps the ARRAY across multiple lines doesn't trip the assertion on a benign reformat; P9 pgTAP test #11 (GRANT EXECUTE) switched from`EXISTS (... WHERE p.proname IN (4 names) ...)`to`SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT p.proname) = 4`— pre-patch`EXISTS`returned TRUE when any single function had the grant; 3 of 4 functions could lose their GRANT and the test would still pass; P10 drift detector now pins`score\s*=\s*round\(`on the running-average math — a future refactor that drops`round(...)`would silently produce float scores in the FLOAT column, breaking the integer-stored-historically contract; P11`update_streak_atomic`gains a 4th CASE arm`WHEN last_active_date > p_today THEN COALESCE(streak_days, 0)`to preserve the streak on clock-skew / DST / timezone-roaming — pre-patch a future`last_active_date`(user traveled west, device clock skew, DST fall-back) fell into the`ELSE 1`reset branch and silently reset the streak; P12`updateSkillProgress` `captureError`extras pass`incomingScore`(clamped) instead of the raw`score`input — Sentry payload now mirrors what the RPC actually saw for diagnostic fidelity on clamp-related errors; P13 CLAUDE.md`\*\*tests\*\*` path references inside backticks are backslash-escaped (`\_\_tests\_\_`) so prettier's markdown formatter doesn't revert them to `\*\*tests\*\*` bold markers on the next format pass (a quirky interaction with prettier's italic-marker normalization that only affects this paragraph's specific punctuation context); P14`activity-rpc-mutations.test.ts` checkCefrPromotion test cases use unique userIds per case (`user-case-12-${level}`, `user-case-13`, `user-case-14`, `user-case-15`, `user-case-16`) so the module-level `lastSkippedBreadcrumb`Map in`activity.ts`cannot dedup-suppress a test's breadcrumb because of a previous case's fingerprint; P15 Case 12 (promotion happy path) converted from a single A1→A2 assertion to a`it.each([[A1,A2],[A2,B1],[B1,B2],[B2,C1],[C1,C2]])`table-driven adjacency matrix — pre-patch a future refactor that hardcoded`p_next_level: "A2"`instead of computing it from`CEFR_ORDER[currentIdx + 1]`would have passed the test; P16 pgTAP test gains a sanity-precheck`IF auth.uid() IS NULL THEN RAISE EXCEPTION 'TEST INFRA FAIL'`immediately after`SET LOCAL request.jwt.claims = '...'`— pre-patch test #10's cross-user defense passed VACUOUSLY when`auth.uid()`returned NULL because`NULL IS DISTINCT FROM '22222222-...'`evaluates to TRUE, raising the auth.uid exception regardless of whether the JWT context was actually installed; the new precheck fails loudly if a future Supabase release changes the JWT setting key; P17`update_skill_progress_atomic`adds an explicit NaN guard`IF p_incoming_score IS NULL OR NOT (p_incoming_score = p_incoming_score) THEN p_incoming_score := 0`before the GREATEST/LEAST clamp —`COALESCE(NaN, 0) = NaN`(NaN is not NULL), so a future caller bypassing the client wrapper could otherwise write NaN into the FLOAT score column; the`NaN ≠ NaN`IEEE 754 idiom catches both NaN and SQL NULL, normalizing to 0. **Deferred (2 pre-existing items not introduced by 12-3):** Phase A race between`incrementDailyActivity`'s `trg_daily_activity_last_active`trigger setting`profiles.last_active_date = today`first and`updateStreak`'s CASE then short-circuiting — Story 12-1 / Story 9-2 hazard; should be filed as a follow-up story. **10 rejected** as noise: cosmetic wasted-write on no-op streak day, midnight test-flake (1ms window), degenerate state hunter self-flagged as non-regression, explicit `updated_at`+ trigger redundancy, invalid SQL would fail deploy, client wrapper return-integer enhancement, mock`data:false` serialization speculation, all-zero-fields guard caller responsibility, auditor's 4 "no action required" LOW findings. +10 net Jest cases (1323 → 1333 — 6 new drift-detector cases from P1/P2/P5/P7/P8/P10/P11/P17 pins + 4 new table-driven adjacency cases from P15 expansion of Case 12). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-3 (post-review-round-1 patches HIGH × 3 + MED × 8 + LOW × 6).

**`RealtimeOrchestrator.start()` race fix — `this.session` populated BEFORE `await session.connect()`:** post-Epic-12.4, audit finding **P2-21** closes architecturally. Pre-12-4 `src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts:1234-1237` assigned `this.session = session` AFTER `await session.connect()` resolved, leaving a microtask window between `ws.onopen → resolve()` (inside `establishConnection()` at `src/lib/realtime.ts:316-346`) and the orchestrator's `await` continuation during which (a) the WebSocket was OPEN, (b) `ws.onmessage` was wired and routing incoming Realtime API events through `this.emit(data) → handleEvent`, (c) OpenAI's `session.updated` ack (and potentially other early events from a very-fast turn) could fire, (d) `handleEvent` ran and referenced `this.session` at 13 sites in handleEvent-reachable paths — all using `this.session?.method()` optional chaining that silently no-op'd when `this.session` was null. The silent-no-op failure mode caused (i) **Story 11-1 tool-call hangs** when `report_correction` / `save_vocabulary` / `note_error_pattern` arrived during the connect window — OpenAI waits forever for a `sendFunctionResult` ack that never lands, (ii) **Story 11-2 barge-in misses on the AI's first utterance** when the user interrupts before `this.session = session` runs — `sendRaw({type:"response.cancel"})` no-ops, (iii) **audio-streaming drops** during the dispose-mid-stream window. Story 12-4 fixes via three coordinated changes: (1) **Assign-before-await:** `this.session = session` is moved BEFORE `await session.connect()` so any event firing during the await window sees a populated reference; the call sequence is now `const session = new RealtimeSession(config); this.session = session; session.on(this.handleEvent); try { await session.connect(); } catch (err) { this.session = null; this.isAiSpeakingMirror = false; this.responseInFlight = false; throw err; }` — the catch path clears the ref + resets synchronous mirrors (Story 12-1 review-round-1 P1 pattern extended to failure recovery). (2) **`safeSessionCall<T>(fn, context)` helper** added as a private method on the orchestrator — a uniform wrapper that null-guards `this.session` and emits an `addBreadcrumb({ category: "realtime", level: "warning", message: "orchestrator-session-null-on-event", data: { feature: "orchestrator-session-null-on-event", context } })` when the ref is null, returning `undefined` instead of silently dropping the method invocation. The pre-12-4 silent-no-op failure mode is now observable in Sentry telemetry — operators can grep for the new feature tag to spot frequency in prod, and any future regression that re-introduces a similar race is detectable. (3) **13 `this.session?.method()` call sites migrated** to `this.safeSessionCall(s => s.method(args), "<context-tag>")`: 10 `sendFunctionResult` sites in `handleFunctionCall` with 5 distinct context tags (`tool-call-save-vocabulary`, `tool-call-note-error-pattern`, `tool-call-report-correction`, `tool-call-unknown`, `tool-call-handler-error`), 2 `sendRaw` sites in `handleSpeechStarted` barge-in (`barge-in-cancel`, `barge-in-truncate`), and 1 `appendAudio` site in the audio-stream subscription callback (`audio-stream`). **Public-API entry points NOT migrated** at `:303` (`dispose` path), `:1261` / `:1274` (`sendText` guard + dispatch), `:1292` (`end` path) — those are called from React event handlers, not from inside `handleEvent`, so the race doesn't apply. The wrapper is a transparent pass-through when `this.session` is non-null (happy-path behavior bit-identical to pre-12-4). Story 9-3 Sentry allowlist contract preserved — one new feature tag `"orchestrator-session-null-on-event"` (34 chars, under 80-char threshold; `context` extras key already allowlisted). The race window is small in practice (~microseconds between `resolve()` and orchestrator continuation) but **deterministically observable** under (i) slow CPU / busy main thread (React Native navigation transition delays the microtask flush), (ii) fast OpenAI response (warm TCP/TLS connection pooling + ~30-50ms RTT can land `session.updated` ack before the orchestrator's continuation runs), (iii) Story 11-2 reconnect interaction (reconnect's `attemptReconnect` re-runs `establishConnection` on the same session ref — the early-assign pattern in `start()` matches the audit-spec'd fix scope; reconnect is Story 11-2's territory and orthogonal). Event-queueing during the (now-narrower) connect window is **out of scope** — early-assign closes the race completely; events arriving in the window are mostly `session.updated` confirmations that `handleEvent`'s switch default-ignores. A future Epic 12.X can add a queue if production telemetry reveals event-loss frequency above background noise. Story 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-X / 11-1 (tool-call protocol — 10 sendFunctionResult sites now route through the helper, happy-path bit-identical) / 11-2 (reconnect + barge-in — 2 sendRaw sites route through the helper; reconnect path uses same session ref) / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 (orchestrator structure — `PHASE_A_SLOT_NAMES`, `INITIAL_STATE`, observer pattern, synchronous-mirror invariants, `isDisposed` short-circuit all unchanged) / 12-2 / 12-3 invariants all hold by construction. Closes audit P2-21 architecturally. Regression-tested in `src/lib/\_\_tests\_\_/realtime-orchestrator-session-race.test.ts` (NEW — 10 Jest cases: 5 drift-detector cases reading `realtime-orchestrator.ts` from disk via a comment-stripped `ORCHESTRATOR_CODE_ONLY` (Story 12-2 P12 lesson — strip block + line comments before regex so JSDoc that mentions the pre-12-4 pattern doesn't trip the drift detector) and asserting the assign-before-await positive guard + the no-late-assign negative guard + the catch-path cleanup contract (`this.session = null` + `isAiSpeakingMirror = false` + `responseInFlight = false`) + the `safeSessionCall` signature + the canonical breadcrumb message; 1 connect-failure cleanup case mocking `RealtimeSession.connect()` to reject and asserting `this.session === null` after the failure (verified via the follow-up `end()` call not invoking `disconnect` on a stale session ref); 2 helper-behavior cases (happy-path: non-null session → method invoked + no null-breadcrumb; null-path: after `end()` → method skipped + canonical breadcrumb fires with `context: "tool-call-save-vocabulary"`); 2 Story-11-1/11-2-preservation cases (report_correction tool-call still routes through helper; barge-in `sendRaw({type:"response.cancel"})` still routes through helper)). +10 net Jest cases (1333 → 1343). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-4. **Story 12-4 review-round-1 patches** (HIGH × 2 + MED × 8 + LOW × 5): P1 audio-stream `safeSessionCall` site restructured — pre-patch the `isConnected` check pre-gated via `this.session?.isConnected` which short-circuited to `undefined` when session was null, making the null-breadcrumb structurally unreachable / dead code. Post-patch: `if (event.data) this.safeSessionCall((s) => { if (s.isConnected) s.appendAudio(...); }, "audio-stream")` — null-guard runs through the helper, `isConnected` reconnect-window-gate stays inside. P2 documentation count drift — said "14 call sites" + "11 sendFunctionResult" + "6 distinct tool-call tags" but `grep -cE` returns **13** (10 sendFunctionResult + 2 sendRaw + 1 appendAudio with 5 tool-call + 2 barge-in + 1 audio-stream = 8 distinct context tags). P3 connect-failure cleanup adds `session.disconnect({reason:"user"})` BEFORE `this.session = null` so half-open WebSocket's `onclose` / `onmessage` handlers don't stay wired to `handleEvent` (late events would otherwise drive state mutations on a "disposed" orchestrator). P4 test Case 6 upgraded from indirect to direct probe — dispatches synthetic tool-call after failure + asserts null-breadcrumb fires + `getState().status === "error"`; drains fire-and-forget `persistConversation` via `setImmediate` to prevent test-boundary leaks. P5 `safeSessionCall` TOCTOU defense — captures `const session = this.session;` BEFORE null check (defense-in-depth for future async-fn migrations). P6 Case 9 setup comment corrected — pre-patch claimed `response.created` sets `responseInFlight = true` but there's no such handler case; updated to inject only the transcript-delta and document the `inflightItemId` OR-gate arm. P7 `session.on(handler)` now wired BEFORE `this.session = session` — synchronous re-entrant code paths see the session WITH its handler already wired. Early-assign still closes the await race because both statements run sync before `await session.connect()`. P8 `session.on(handler)` wrapped inside the same inner try/catch as `await session.connect()` — a synchronous throw from `Set.add` OOM / future SDK validation is handled by the same cleanup path instead of leaving a half-initialized session. P9 `safeSessionCall` JSDoc documents the synchronous-fn invariant — the helper returns `T | undefined`; async `fn` would silently drop the Promise, re-introducing the silent-no-op failure mode. P10 drift-detector regex fragility — Case 2 negative-guard separator widened to `[\s\S]{0,300}?` for formatter resilience; Case 3 try-block separator loosened to `[\s\S]*?` for no-semi mode + additional-statements resilience; added Case 3b (P3 disconnect invariant) and Case 3c (P7+P8 ordering invariant). P11 "7 distinct context tags" corrected to "8" (5 tool-call + 2 barge-in + 1 audio-stream). P12 "36 chars" corrected to "34 chars" for `"orchestrator-session-null-on-event"`. P13 breadcrumb `message` field rewritten from categorical-duplicate to human-readable `"Session ref null when handler dispatched"`; `feature` extras key remains the categorical Sentry tag for grep. Test assertions updated to filter by `data.feature` (Story 9-3 contract) instead of `message`. P14 test `user` field cast `as User` instead of `as never` for minimal type-checking against User-shape changes. +3 net Jest cases (1343 → 1346): Case 3b + Case 3c drift-detector pins + Case 6b connect-failure-disconnect runtime case. **Deferred (4 pre-existing items not introduced by 12-4):** partial mirror reset in inner catch; shallow `Object.freeze` `getState()` (Story 12-1 P15 pre-existing); `start()` public-API `sendText` narrowing fragility (spec out-of-scope); `session.on()` unsubscribe closure discarded (partially addressed by P3). **5 rejected** as noise: ESM-future-fragility speculation, barge-in-truncate closure pattern is correct, Case 8 `end()` vs `dispose()` coupling intentional, partial-mirror-reset (also deferred), breadcrumb `feature` duplicates `message` (covered by P13). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-4 (post-review-round-1 patches HIGH × 2 + MED × 8 + LOW × 5).

**`ExpoPlayAudioStream` lifecycle — singleton manager with reference counting:** post-Epic-12.5, audit finding **P1-19** closes architecturally + Epic 12 AC at [`shippable-roadmap.md` line 220](_bmad-output/planning-artifacts/shippable-roadmap.md) ("audio works after 5 successive screen mount/unmount cycles") is verified by the 5-cycle smoke test. Pre-12-5 [`src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts:307`](src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts#L307) called `ExpoPlayAudioStream.destroy()` on every orchestrator dispose. The native module from [`@mykin-ai/expo-audio-stream`](https://github.com/mykin-ai/expo-audio-stream) is a **process-wide singleton** (every import resolves to the same JS proxy backed by ONE iOS `AVAudioEngine` / one Android `AudioRecord` instance), so calling `.destroy()` on conversation end tore down the underlying native engine — leaving the NEXT orchestrator's `startAudioStreaming()` calling `requestPermissionsAsync` / `setSoundConfig` / `startRecording` on a destroyed singleton — which silently failed (no subscription, no audio data flowing, `onAudioStream` callback never fires) UNTIL the app was fully reloaded. The user-facing symptom: voice conversations work the FIRST time after app launch but every subsequent conversation has silent recording + silent AI TTS playback. The misleading API-name collision (`destroy` ≠ `cleanup`) caused the bug: `destroy()` is for app-shutdown teardown, NOT for per-screen lifecycle. Story 12-5 lands a **3-part fix**: (1) **new `src/lib/audio-stream-manager.ts` module** (~125 lines including JSDoc) — exports `acquireAudioStream()` (increments module-level `let refCount = 0` + returns the `ExpoPlayAudioStream` singleton reference), `releaseAudioStream()` (decrements; on last release fires `stopRecording().catch(() => {})` + `stopSound().catch(() => {})` best-effort — **never `destroy()`**), `getAudioStreamRefCountForTests()` test-only inspector, `__resetAudioStreamManagerForTests()` test-only reset with `NODE_ENV !== "test"` runtime guard (Story 12-2 P11 pattern). Defensive release-when-zero emits `addBreadcrumb({category:"audio", level:"warning", message:"Audio stream released when no acquires outstanding", data:{feature:"audio-stream-release-when-zero"}})` and exits without decrementing (no negative-state pollution). Pattern alignment: module-level `let refCount` mirrors Story 12-2's `bootstrapAuth()` one-call-guard (`let bootstrapState`) + Story 9-6's `flushWriteQueue` idempotency (`let inFlight`). (2) **`src/lib/realtime-orchestrator.ts` modifications** — new `private acquireWasCalled = false` instance field for matched-pair tracking (Story 12-1 synchronous-mirror pattern applied to lifecycle); `acquireAudioStream(); this.acquireWasCalled = true;` runs as the first 2 statements of `startAudioStreaming()` (line 449-450); the pre-12-5 `ExpoPlayAudioStream.destroy();` line is **DELETED** (Story 10-2 / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 / 12-2 / 12-3 / 12-4 "delete don't alias" pattern) and replaced with `if (this.acquireWasCalled) { this.acquireWasCalled = false; void releaseAudioStream(); }` so dispose only releases when acquire actually ran (defends against `start()` throwing BEFORE `startAudioStreaming()` runs — without this guard the refcount would go negative on every failed start). `start()`'s reset block now resets `this.acquireWasCalled = false` alongside `isAiSpeakingMirror` + `responseInFlight` (Story 12-1 P1 pattern). The **7 per-operation `ExpoPlayAudioStream.X(...)` call sites are UNCHANGED** (lines 459, 468, 473, 516, 740, 847, 1487 — `requestPermissionsAsync` + `setSoundConfig` + `startRecording` + `stopRecording` in `stopAudioStreaming` + `playSound` for audio playback + 2× `stopSound` for barge-in + end-of-conversation) — they continue using the singleton directly because they're idempotent per-call operations, not lifecycle hooks. Only the lifecycle changes go through the manager. (3) **Tests**: `src/lib/__tests__/audio-stream-manager.test.ts` (NEW — 10 Jest cases: refcount happy paths × 4 [initial 0 + 1-acquire/1-release + 3-acquire/3-release + intermediate-releases-don't-cleanup] + NEVER-destroy negative guards × 2 [5-cycle smoke test = the canonical Epic 12 AC line 220 verification + drift detector reads `audio-stream-manager.ts` from disk and asserts comment-stripped source contains NO `.destroy(` invocations] + defensive guards × 2 [release-when-zero breadcrumb + `__resetAudioStreamManagerForTests` throws on `NODE_ENV !== "test"`] + test-only inspector × 1 + best-effort cleanup × 1 [stopRecording/stopSound throwing doesn't propagate]) + `src/lib/__tests__/realtime-orchestrator-audio-lifecycle.test.ts` (NEW — 6 Jest cases: drift detector × 3 [comment-stripped negative guard against `ExpoPlayAudioStream.destroy()` + positive guards on `acquireAudioStream()` import/call + `releaseAudioStream()` gated on `acquireWasCalled`] + lifecycle correctness × 3 [1:1 acquire/release per orchestrator instance + start-failure-before-startAudioStreaming = NO unmatched release + double-dispose calls release EXACTLY ONCE via Story 12-1 P7 `isDisposed` short-circuit]). Sentry allowlist contract preserved (Story 9-3): one new feature tag `"audio-stream-release-when-zero"` (33 chars; well under 80-char threshold); no new extras keys. Story 9-3 / 9-4 / 9-5 / 9-6 / 9-7 / 9-8 / 9-9 / 9-10 / 10-X / 11-1 (tool-call protocol — orthogonal) / 11-2 (barge-in's `void ExpoPlayAudioStream.stopSound()` at line 819 is a per-operation call, NOT lifecycle — unchanged) / 11-3 / 11-4 / 11-5 / 11-6 / 11-7 / 11-8 / 12-1 (orchestrator structure — `PHASE_A_SLOT_NAMES`, `INITIAL_STATE`, observer pattern, dispose() cleanup ORDER [timer → subscription → session → audio → subscribers], synchronous-mirror invariants all unchanged) / 12-2 / 12-3 / 12-4 invariants all hold by construction. Closes audit P1-19 architecturally + Epic 12 AC line 220. +16 net Jest cases (1346 → 1362). Verified 2026-05-13, story 12-5. **Story 12-5 review-round-1 patches** (HIGH × 2 + MED × 7 + LOW × 4; P8 + P15 reverted as noise — see below): P1 `start()` reset block leak — pre-patch the `acquireWasCalled = false` reset cleared the flag WITHOUT firing the matching release, so a `start()` retry after a partial prior start (or an `end()`→`start()` recycle) leaked one refcount per cycle and the singleton stayed open for ghost consumers; post-patch the reset block fires `releaseAudioStream()` BEFORE clearing the flag whenever `acquireWasCalled === true`; P2 `releaseAudioStream` snapshot-after-await defense against the concurrent-orchestrators race — pre-patch orchestrator A's release-to-0 awaited `stopRecording()`, during which orchestrator B's synchronous `acquireAudioStream()` landed (refCount 0→1), then A continued to fire `stopSound()` killing B's freshly-started session; post-patch the cleanup arm re-checks `refCount !== 0` after `stopRecording` resolves and ABANDONS the remaining cleanup chain if a peer acquired during the await; P3 new test (`Case 7`) verifies post-acquire throw (e.g., `requestPermissionsAsync` rejection AFTER the synchronous acquire ran) still releases on dispose — the synchronous-acquire invariant means `acquireWasCalled` is always set before any await can throw; P4 new test (`Case 11` + `Case 12`) verifies the concurrent-orchestrators contract — Case 11 directly exercises the P2 race (deferred `stopRecording` + mid-await peer acquire → `stopSound` is NOT called); Case 12 runs 5 interleaved acquire/release cycles across multiple consumers + asserts `destroy` never fires (Epic 12 AC #4); P5 `__resetAudioStreamManagerForTests()` called in `beforeEach` of the 12-1 (`realtime-orchestrator.test.ts`) and 12-4 (`realtime-orchestrator-session-race.test.ts`) test files so module-level refcount state from a prior test doesn't bleed across suite boundaries; P6 JSDoc top-of-file documents `end()`→`dispose()` duplicate-stop tolerance (`dispose()` is idempotent via Story 12-1 P7 `isDisposed`; release-when-zero breadcrumb catches unmatched second calls without negative-state); P7 JSDoc documents the **synchronous-acquire invariant** — callers MUST NOT `await` between `acquireAudioStream()` and the `acquireWasCalled = true` bookkeeping write; violating it is a refcount-leak hazard; the arrow-function wrapper captures the NAME and resolves at call-time (post-TDZ). +5 net Jest cases (1362 → 1367): P3 Case 7 + P1 Case 8 in audio-lifecycle file + P4 Case 11 + Case 12 in audio-stream-manager file + P10 hook-budget audio-stream-manager negative guard.
